        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.9b04088"><meta property="og:title" content="Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/acsami.9b04088.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="In recent times, few-layer black phosphorus (BP) has attracted tremendous attention as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its particular two-dimensional structure, good electron conductivity, and high theoretical capacity. The main disadvantages of BP-based materials are the lower practical specific capacity of the BP-based composite than expectation because of the low P atom utilization and the structural fracture due to the large volume expansion that occurs during sodiation/desodiation cycles. In this work, we report a ternary composite comprising BP, graphite, and polyaniline (BP-G/PANI) with a BP mass content of ∼65 wt %. The ternary composite provides an optimized ion pathway (electrolyte → PANI → BP-G → BP), which reduces the charge transfer resistance of the electrode. Also, further ex situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy measurements demonstrate that the presence of graphite in the BP-G composite allows a deep sodiation of BP and also leads to a higher sodiation/desodiation reversibility. In addition, the uniformly coated PANI also restricts the huge volume expansion of the BP electrode through discharge/charge processes, which promise the stable cycling performance of BP-G/PANI. Thus, our composite shows a high reversible gravimetric capacity of 1530 mAh gcompo.–1 at 0.25 A g–1 and a capacity retention of 520 mAh gcompo.–1 after 1000 cycles at a high current density of 4 A g–1."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/acsami.9b04088.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da90f79dcdb325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da90f79dcdb325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '99f28ae0-75e9-4ad4-9bea-9f9c6d0bde5b'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da90f79dcdb325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synergy of Black Phosphorus–Graphite–Polyaniline-Based Ternary Composites for Stable High Reversible Capacity Na-Ion Battery Anodes", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b04088", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Chemistry, Chinese Academy of Sciences (CAS), Beijing 100190, China</div></div><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Li-jun++Wan" data-id="article_author_search">Li-jun Wan</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D16656%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHongchang%2BJin%252C%2BTaiming%2BZhang%252C%2BChenghao%2BChuang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D11%26issueNum%3D18%26contentID%3Dacsami.9b04088%26title%3DSynergy%2Bof%2BBlack%2BPhosphorus%25E2%2580%2593Graphite%25E2%2580%2593Polyaniline-Based%2BTernary%2BComposites%2Bfor%2BStable%2BHigh%2BReversible%2BCapacity%2BNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D16661%26publicationDate%3DMay%2B2019" Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/medium/am-2019-04088f_0005.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b04088&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">In recent times, few-layer black phosphorus (BP) has attracted tremendous attention as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to its particular two-dimensional structure, good electron conductivity, and high theoretical capacity. The main disadvantages of BP-based materials are the lower practical specific capacity of the BP-based composite than expectation because of the low P atom utilization and the structural fracture due to the large volume expansion that occurs during sodiation/desodiation cycles. In this work, we report a ternary composite comprising BP, graphite, and polyaniline (BP-G/PANI) with a BP mass content of ∼65 wt %. The ternary composite provides an optimized ion pathway (electrolyte → PANI → BP-G → BP), which reduces the charge transfer resistance of the electrode. Also, further ex situ X-ray absorption spectroscopy measurements demonstrate that the presence of graphite in the BP-G composite allows a deep sodiation of BP and also leads to a higher sodiation/desodiation reversibility. In addition, the uniformly coated PANI also restricts the huge volume expansion of the BP electrode through discharge/charge processes, which promise the stable cycling performance of BP-G/PANI. Thus, our composite shows a high reversible gravimetric capacity of 1530 mAh g<sub>compo.</sub><sup>–1</sup> at 0.25 A g<sup>–1</sup> and a capacity retention of 520 mAh g<sub>compo.</sub><sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles at a high current density of 4 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D16656%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DHongchang%2BJin%252C%2BTaiming%2BZhang%252C%2BChenghao%2BChuang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D11%26issueNum%3D18%26contentID%3Dacsami.9b04088%26title%3DSynergy%2Bof%2BBlack%2BPhosphorus%25E2%2580%2593Graphite%25E2%2580%2593Polyaniline-Based%2BTernary%2BComposites%2Bfor%2BStable%2BHigh%2BReversible%2BCapacity%2BNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D16661%26publicationDate%3DMay%2B2019" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2019 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291442&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Anode materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Anode%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Anode materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291331&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Composites" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Composites" class="article__tags__link">Composites</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291203&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Plastics" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Plastics" class="article__tags__link">Plastics</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292475&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Polymers" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Polymers" class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Material&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode%20material">anode material</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Black+Phosphorus&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_black%20phosphorus">black phosphorus</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Phosphorus+Utilization&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_phosphorus%20utilization">phosphorus utilization</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High+Reversible+Capacity&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high%20reversible%20capacity">high reversible capacity</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a promising candidate to replace lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale energy storage considering sodium’s superiority in cost and abundance. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> However, Na ions suffer a sluggish electrochemistry kinetic process when intercalating/deintercalating in the electrode compared with Li ions, which leads to the low reversible capacity and cyclic performance of cathode and anode materials. Therefore, to overcome this disadvantage, a number of cathode materials with performances comparable to those of LIBs have been reported for SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2 ref3 ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2 ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 2 to 4">(2−4)</a> Besides, many different anode materials have also been investigated, such as carbonaceous materials, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5 ref6 ref7'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 5 to 7">(5−7)</a> transition-metal oxides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8 ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 8 and 9">(8,9)</a> metal sulfides, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 10 and 11">(10,11)</a> organic salts, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref13'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13" aria-label="reference 12 and 13">(12,13)</a> and alloy-type material. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20" aria-label="reference 14 to 20">(14−20)</a> Although much progress has been made, anode materials with high reversible capacity and long lifespan are still the research hotspot in both academia and industry for SIBs, owing to the growing demands for high-energy and low-price electrical power sources.</div><div class="NLM_p">Recently, black phosphorus (BP) has drawn much attention owing to its high theoretical capacity of 2600 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> and a low working potential (0.3 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). Furthermore, thanks to the unique two-dimensional puckered honeycomb structure, BP displays many features, such as a high electrical conductivity of ∼300 S m<sup>–1</sup>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> a larger interlayer spacing than graphite (3.08 vs 1.86 Å) that facilitates the intercalation of both Li<sup>+</sup> (0.76 Å) and Na<sup>+</sup> (1.02 Å), and a fast Na-ion diffusion capability along the zigzag direction ensuring a high level of sodiation for phosphorus atoms. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> Thus, a number of BP-based composites were synthesized for SIB anodes. Cui et al. first reported a phosphorene/graphene composite with a capacity of 1179 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (calculated based on the total mass of composite, 93.8% P utilization) at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup>, which remained 516 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles at 8 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Amine and co-workers prepared a BP/Ketjenblack/CNT composite, which delivered a capacity of 1505 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>–1</sup> (77.3% P utilization) and a capacity retention of 1190 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1.3 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> Dou et al. demonstrated a functionalized few-layer BP, and the electrode displayed a discharge capacity of 1597 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (69% P utilization) and a capacity retention of 1050 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> Although these works led to noteworthy enhancement in the reversible capacity of BP-based materials, the cycling stability of high-capacity anodes over a long term at high current densities needs to be improved urgently.</div><div class="NLM_p">Specifically, the main reasons for the low capacity and poor lifespan at high current density are as follows. First, the utilization of P determines the reversible capacity of BP-based materials during sodiation/desodiation processes. Pristine BP shows a low BP utilization of &lt;70% due to its inferior wettability (in the electrolyte), which hinders the ion diffusion from an electrolyte into an electrode. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> Second, phosphorus suffers huge volume expansion (∼490%) after the sodiation process, and the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) generated on the surface of fractured BP, which leads to the contact loss with the current collector, results in the fast capacity fading. Therefore, it is critical to find an approach to enhance P utilization and conquer the huge volume expansion, which could achieve stable high reversible capacity of BP-based material for SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this work, we present a BP-based composite with a rational design containing few-layer BP flakes, graphite, and polyaniline (BP-G/PANI) to be applied as an SIB anode to realize both high reversible capacity and a stable cyclic performance at high current densities. The electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) results demonstrate that graphite in the BP-G hybrid reduces the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) compared with the pristine BP. In addition, the presence of graphite also enhances the P utilization during the sodiation/desodiation process, which is represented through X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) measurements. Furthermore, a uniform PANI coating layer shows swelling properties in the electrolyte, which ensures an efficient access of Na ions to the BP-G hybrid and enables high reversible capacity at high rate. PANI also accommodates the volume expansion and provides a conductive network, which lead to the stability of our composite during long-term sodiation/desodiation cycles. Thus, an optimized ion pathway (electrolyte → PANI → BP-G → BP) was constructed. Benefiting from the well-designed ternary structure, our BP-G/PANI composite delivered a high reversible capacity of 1530 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (90% P utilization) at a current density of 0.25 A g<sup>–1</sup> (here, we calculate the capacity taking the total mass of the composite into account). Most significantly, the reversible capacity still remains 520 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles at a high current density of 4 A g<sup>–1</sup> with an extremely low capacity fading rate of 0.024%. The superior performance of BP-G/PANI can be ascribed to the rational structure of BP-G/PANI with reduced <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>, enhanced P utilization, and long-term stability.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a> describes the structural characterization of BP-G/PANI. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a shows the different steps in the fabrication of the ternary composite BP–graphite–PANI; the ternary structure conquers the volume changes of BP during (de)sodiating processes and thereby prevents a loss of contact of BP-G with the current collector during battery cycling. Few-layer BP was used as the starting material (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>), and the BP-G particles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>) were well coated with PANI (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b,c). Also, the schematic in the right of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a describes the unique structure of BP-G/PANI. PANI offers a Na-ion pathway between the electrolyte and active material (BP-G) and the electron conductive network, and the graphite in the BP-G reduces the ion charge transfer resistance. Raman spectrum (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b) shows intense bands at 363, 440, and 467 cm<sup>–1</sup>, which represent the feature peaks of BP. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Two broad peaks are also seen at 1323 and 1604 cm<sup>–1</sup>, ascribed to the D and G bands of the graphite, respectively, and two low-intensity broad peaks appear at 850 and 1200 cm<sup>–1</sup>, which are characteristic of PANI. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns show characteristic diffraction peaks of BP at 2θ values of 16.8, 26.5, 34.1, and 34.9° in both samples (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c), and a broad peak originating from PANI appears at around 22° (black). Raman spectra and XRD pattern thus confirm that BP remains intact while forming the composite BP-G/PANI. The microstructure of BP-G/PANI was characterized by transmission electron microscopy (TEM). Our BP-G/PANI sample is made up of small BP-G particles coated by the cross-linked polymer PANI; the HRTEM image shows a detailed view of the edge of graphene where a lattice spacing of 4.41 Å is measured, corresponding to a zigzag edge of BP (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> A graphite lattice plane with a spacing of 2.06 Å is also present. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> The amorphous part outside BP and graphite corresponds to PANI (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>e). Furthermore, TEM mapping images show that C, P, and N are evenly distributed in the BP-G/PANI particle (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>f–i).</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/medium/am-2019-04088f_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Structure characterization of BP-based materials. (a) Schematic diagram of the sodiation of BP-G and BP-G/PANI electrodes. (b) Raman spectra and (c) XRD patterns of BP-G/PANI and BP. (d) TEM and (e) HRTEM images of BP-G/PANI. (f–i) TEM elemental mapping images of BP-G/PANI.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b04088&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To further investigate the effect of graphite on the improved P utilization and the effect of PANI on the improved cycling stability, first, we recorded X-ray absorption spectra to understand the P state in BP and BP-G (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a). The absorption edge of BP-G is at 2145.7 eV, which is higher than that of BP (2145.5 eV) due to the strong charge transfer from P to C owing to the much higher electron affinity of C (1.262 eV) than P (0.746 eV). Furthermore, we test the ex situ XAS of BP and BP-G at different states of charge. The P <i>K</i>-edge of BP-G is up-shifted to 2146.0 eV and a pre-edge appears after sodiation (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b), indicating the formation of Na<i><sub>x</sub></i>P (1 &lt; <i>x</i> &lt; 3) by sodiation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> However, the P <i>K</i>-edge of BP shows no change after discharging to 0.001 V (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c), which means that the electron density of BP is not altered during the discharging step. Interestingly, if the BP-G electrode is charged back to 2.0 V, the P <i>K</i>-edge shifts back to its initial state. In contrast, the BP-G electrode displays a significant change after discharging due to the presence of graphite, which enables the high utilization of BP during sodiation/desodiation processes. We further test the wettability of BP and BP-G electrodes in the electrolyte (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>). The contact angle (electrolyte) of the BP electrode is 19°, whereas the BP-G electrode shows the contact angle of almost 0°, which delivers the great wettability of BP-G with the electrolyte after the addition of graphite. The superior wettability of BP-G delivers a better contact of the electrolyte and enables the fast transfer of Na<sup>+</sup> in the electrode. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> The results give important evidence to demonstrate the function of graphite in the BP-G sample.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/medium/am-2019-04088f_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Function of graphite and PANI in a BP-based composite during the discharge/charge process. (a) P <i>K</i>-edge XAS spectra of BP and BP-G. Ex situ XAS P <i>K</i>-edge spectra of (b) BP-G and (c) BP. Cross-sectional SEM images of (d) BP-G/PANI and (e) BP-G electrodes before and after three cycles.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b04088&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Next, we prepared BP-G/PANI and BP-G electrodes of similar thickness and obtained thickness evolution of the electrode in the desodiated state before and after three cycles through scanning electron microscope (SEM) images. The BP-G/PANI electrode (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d) shows a 19% thickness increase after three cycles without any apparent structural damage to the electrode. In contrast, the BP-G electrode (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>e) undergoes a 60% increase in thickness and develops cracks, which are clearly seen on the electrode. In addition, these results demonstrate that the PANI coating mitigates the detrimental effects of volume changes in the BP-based electrode, resulting in a longer cycle life for BP-G/PANI.</div><div class="NLM_p">Additionally, a PANI mat was prepared using a tablet machine to investigate the swelling property in the NaClO<sub>4</sub>/PC electrolyte. As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>, the PANI mat shows 18% thickness increase after filtration in the electrolyte, which means that PANI can conquer the volume changes of BP and provide a Na-ion pathway from the electrolyte to most of the active materials (BP-G). Because the solvation of Na<sup>+</sup> in the electrolyte is easier than that of Li<sup>+</sup>, it results in the low <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of BP in SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> Thus, ensuring the full contact of the electrolyte to the electrode will be critical to increase capacity at high current density. Also, swelled PANI could ensure the efficient access of Na ions in the electrolyte to BP-G, which benefits the improvement of the reversible capacity of BP-G/PANI at high current density.</div><div class="NLM_p">Owing to its unique structure, BP-G/PANI has a high reversible capacity of 1530 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.25 A g<sup>–1</sup>. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a shows the voltage profiles of BP-G/PANI at different current densities in the range of 0.25–4 A g<sup>–1</sup> within the voltage window of 0.01–2 V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). The galvanostatic discharge/charge profile is shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5</a>; the initial Coulombic efficiency (CE) is 51%, which is very close to that of the previous reports (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>), and this irreversible capacity was generated from the formation of the SEI in the voltage range of 1.2–0.6 V. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> The reversible capacity of BP-G/PANI is 1530 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (calculated based on the total mass of the composite) and is 2350 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> when considering only the mass of BP, which corresponds to 90% BP utilization. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) was performed at the scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> in the voltage range of 0.01–2 V to further understand the sodiation/desodiation of BP-G/PANI (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>). Because of the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> and alloying with P (Na<sub>x</sub>P generation, 0 &lt; <i>x</i> &lt; 3), a cathodic peak appeared at 0.4 V, and two anodic peaks at 0.54 and 0.7 V corresponding to desodiation from the reduced species are observed. These three main peaks are also seen in the second cycle, representing the good reversibility of the BP-G/PANI anode.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/medium/am-2019-04088f_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Sodium storage capability of BP-G/PANI. (a) Discharge/charge profiles and (b) rate performances of BP-G/PANI. (c) Cycling stability and Coulombic efficiencies of BP, BP/PANI, BP-G, and BP-G/PANI at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (d) <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of BP, BP-G, and BP-G/PANI. (e) Cycling stability and Coulombic efficiency of BP-G/PANI at 4 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b04088&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The BP-G/PANI anode still delivers a capacity of 1300 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (85%, capacity retention) at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Moreover, the electrode shows capacity retentions of 1070 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (70%), 920 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (60%), and 690 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (45%) even at higher rates of 1, 2.5, and 4 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b), respectively. To test the role of the BP–graphite–PANI ternary structure in its electrochemical performance, similar measurements were also carried out for BP and BP-G electrodes as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S7 and S8</a>. The BP electrode delivers a low capacity of 270 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Besides, for the BP-G electrode, a high capacity of 1830 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (higher than that of BP and BP-G/PANI) is obtained at the start, but this value decreases to 200 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after just 47 cycles. We also tested the capacity contribution of graphite (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>). Graphite delivers a reversible capacity of 25 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, and considering that the mass content of graphite in the BP-G/PANI composite is around 16%, the capacity contribution of graphite is negligible. Thus, the reversible capacity of BP-G/PANI was almost contributed by the BP. The CV profile of BP-G shows features similar to BP-G/PANI (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10</a>), whereas for the BP electrode, the anodic peaks nearly disappear, indicating the poor utilization of BP after the first sodiation (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>). Also, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) of electrodes was carried out before electrochemical testing as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d. The EIS results display that BP-G/PANI shows a charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) of 9.8 Ω lower than that of BP (31.3 Ω) and BP-G (23.1 Ω) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12</a>) based on the modified Randles equivalent circuit. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> These results may enable our BP-G/PANI composite with excellent performance, which benefits from the full contact of the electrolyte to the anode material and insertion/extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> in the electrode. The following electrochemistry test also verifies this conclusion. BP-G/PANI delivers a more stable cycling performance with a capacity retention of 1120 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c) and a higher Coulombic efficiency. BP-G/PANI thus shows an impressive performance with ultrastable cyclic capability at a high rate of 4 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a reversible capacity of 520 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1000 cycles (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>e).</div><div class="NLM_p">Thus, we conclude by comparing the reversible capacities of BP-G and BP in the first tens of cycles that the presence of graphite in BP-G enhances the utilization of BP (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c, black and blue dots) and by comparing the reversible capacities of BP-G/PANI and BP-G the presence of the PANI coating even when leading to a lower initial capacity (as compared to BP-G) effectively improves the cycling stability of the BP-based composite (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c, red and black dots). In addition, by comparing this work with previous works, the BP-G/PANI composite still shows the better cycle performance (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>).</div><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a> shows the structure of BP-G/PANI after 100 sodiation/desodiation cycles. It is seen that a large number of particles with diameter ∼10 nm are formed on the electrode following cycling (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a). We obtained six HRTEM images of small particles located at the edges of BP-G/PANI (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b–g). Except in the image corresponding to the purple square area, no lattice fringes of BP are seen (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b). However, the cycled BP electrode still shows obvious lattice fringes after 100 cycles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S13</a>), which confirms the high utilization of BP during discharge/charge processes with the addition of graphite in the BP-G/PANI. Besides, these results also demonstrated the cracking process of BP, which provided an extra solid/electrolyte interface to form SEI and led to the low initial CE of BP-based material. In addition, the PANI coating is key to mitigating the effects of the large volume change and maintaining the activity of BP-G during cycling. From the TEM elemental maps shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>h–k, even after several cycles, phosphorus is still enveloped by PANI. As a comparison, BP-G shows disorder distribution after 100 cycles according to the TEM images without the PANI coating (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S14</a>), which points to the stable cycling performance of the BP-G/PANI composite during long discharge/charge cycles at the high current density of 4 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/medium/am-2019-04088f_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Structure of BP-G/PANI after discharge/charge processes. (a) TEM image of BP-G/PANI after 100 cycles. (b–g) HRTEM images taken at the different positions marked by squares in panel (a). (h–k) Elemental mapping images of BP-G/PANI after 100 cycles.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/asset/images/large/am-2019-04088f_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b04088&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i4">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">We have designed a ternary BP-G/PANI composite with high reversible capacity and rate performance and ultralong cycle life when used as an SIB anode. The presence of graphite and swollen PANI in BP-G/PANI reduces charge transfer resistance compared with the pristine BP due to the optimized Na-ion migration pathway from the electrolyte to the BP surface, which further enhances the P utilization to around 90% during the sodiation/desodiation process. In addition, PANI also enhanced the structure stability of BP and limited the volume expansion of the electrode during the alloy reaction to form Na<sub>3</sub>P. The simple synthesis process and the superior electrochemical performance of our BP–graphite–PANI ternary composite can be successfully applied to achieve high-energy-density SIBs.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i5">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec4_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6"> Synthesis of BP-G/PANI Composites</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Bulk black phosphorus was prepared using a low-pressure transport method according to our previous work. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> A 10 mg L<sup>–1</sup> dispersion of BP in DMF was prepared by sonication to obtain few-layer BP that was dried and mixed with graphite powder at a BP/G mass ratio of 8:2. The mixture was ball-milled in argon for 12 h to produce the BP-G hybrid. This BP-G hybrid (50 mg) was dispersed in an aqueous solution containing 1 mM aniline and 5 mM phytic acid (solution A) with the assistance of sonication for 1 min. Solution B, containing 1.25 mM ammonium persulfate dissolved in deionized (DI) water, was added dropwise to solution A followed by sonication for 1 min. The mixture was then kept in an ice bath for 5 h before filtration and washing with DI water to yield BP-G/PANI. After weighing the final product, the P content in BP-G/PANI was about 65 wt %. The BP/PANI was synthesized in the same process as a control sample.</div></div><div id="sec4_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7"> Ex Situ XAS Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The P K-edge X-ray absorption was measured using the beamline 16A1 under a chamber pressure &lt;10<sup>–7</sup> Pa at the NSRRC, Hsinchu. The ex situ XAS spectra were recorded at the P K-edge on BP and BP-G electrodes at different states of charge.</div></div><div id="sec4_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8"> Structural Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">SEM images were obtained with a JEOL JSM 6700F instrument. TEM, STEM, and elemental maps were acquired with a JEOL JEM-2100F instrument. Raman spectra were recorded using a Renishaw inVia with 532 nm incident laser excitation. XRD patterns were obtained from a Smart Lab 9 kW X-ray diffraction instrument (Rigaku, Japan).</div></div><div id="sec4_4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i9" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i9"> Electrochemical Measurements</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The electrodes were prepared by mixing 80 wt % active material with 10 wt % Ketjenblack and 10 wt % poly(vinylidenefluoride) (PVDF) to form a slurry, which was coated onto a copper foil (13 μm thick) and dried at 50 °C for 24 h under vacuum (active material loading: 0.8–1.2 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>). The half cells were fabricated with a cathode of the BP composite material, an anode of Na metal, a glass fiber separator, and an electrolyte containing 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> in propylene carbonate (PC) with 5% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC). The charge/discharge tests were performed with a LANDTE battery test system with a voltage window of 0.01–2.0 V, and a voltage window of 0.001–2.0 V was used for XAS measurements. Cyclic voltammetry (0.01–2.0 V) and EIS were carried out by Princeton Applied Research analytical equipment (PARSTAT MC).</div></div><div id="sec4_5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i10" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i10"> Other Characterizations</h3><div class="NLM_p last">For the swelling test of PANI, the PANI powder (60 mg) was pressed into pellets with a diameter of 12 mm under 10 M Pa for 5 min using a tablet machine. Then, the obtained PANI pellet was immersed in the electrolyte for 12 h. The thickness of the PANI pellet before and after immersion in the electrolyte was measured by the optical microscope. The contact angle was measured at room temperature (SL200B, Solon Tech Co., Ltd., Shanghai, China).</div></div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.9b04088" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.9b04088</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">SEM and TEM images of BP, BP-G, and BP-/PANI; optical images of PANI; CV data; EIS data; galvanostatic discharge–charge data (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b04088/suppl_file/am9b04088_si_001.pdf">am9b04088_si_001.pdf (1.03 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b04088" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A 3.8-V earth-abundant sodium battery electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Barpanda, Prabeer; Oyama, Gosuke; Nishimura, Shin-ichi; Chung, Sai-Cheong; Yamada, Atsuo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable lithium batteries have ushered the wireless revolution over last two decades and are now matured to enable green automobiles.  However, the growing concern on scarcity and large-scale applications of lithium resources have steered effort to realize sustainable sodium-ion batteries, Na and Fe being abundant and low-cost charge carrier and redox center, resp.  However, their performance is limited owing to low operating voltage and sluggish kinetics.  Here we report a hitherto-unknown material with entirely new compn. and structure with the first alluaudite-type sulfate framework, Na2Fe2(SO4)3, registering the highest-ever Fe3+/Fe2+ redox potential at 3.8 V (vs. Na, and hence 4.1 V vs. Li) along with fast rate kinetics.  Rare-metal-free Na-ion rechargeable battery system compatible with the present Li-ion battery is now in realistic scope without sacrificing high energy d. and high power, and paves way for discovery of new earth-abundant sustainable cathodes for large-scale batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_sUr2Jpgw1LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhsh73dYPoX3Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVShs77L&amp;md5=20951f27b1483820983947a5d84d607f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms6280"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Manganese Hexacyanomanganate Open Framework as a High-Capacity Positive Electrode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">5280</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms6280</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2014%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DH.-W.%2BLee%26author%3DR.%2BY.%2BWang%26author%3DM.%2BPasta%26author%3DS.%2BW.%2BLee%26author%3DN.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26title%3DManganese%2BHexacyanomanganate%2BOpen%2BFramework%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Capacity%2BPositive%2BElectrode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms6280&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b04088&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms6280&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Manganese hexacyanomanganate open framework as a high-capacity positive electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Hyun-Wook; Wang, Richard Y.; Pasta, Mauro; Lee, Seok Woo; Liu, Nian; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5280</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potential applications of sodium-ion batteries in grid-scale energy storage, portable electronics and elec. vehicles have revitalized research interest in these batteries.  However, the performance of sodium-ion electrode materials has not been competitive with that of lithium-ion electrode materials.  Here we present sodium manganese hexacyanomanganate (Na2MnII[MnII(CN)6]), an open-framework crystal structure material, as a viable pos. electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  We demonstrate a high discharge capacity of 209 mAh g-1 at C/5 (40 mA g-1) and excellent capacity retention at high rates in a propylene carbonate electrolyte.  We provide chem. and structural evidence for the unprecedented storage of 50% more sodium cations than previously thought possible during electrochem. cycling.  These results represent a step forward in the development of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodYRgprGozjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTVlxWaAmUIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVemsrg%253D&amp;md5=24c6dc57b45017370f872c3c6723f4c4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C6CP00651E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jache, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Binder, J. Chem. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14299</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14316</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
