                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comparative study on the impact of different glymes and their derivatives as electrolyte solvents for graphite co-intercalation electrodes in lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jache, Birte; Binder, Jan Oliver; Abe, Takeshi; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14299-14316</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PPCPFQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1463-9076</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium has recently sparked considerable interest in sodium-ion batteries (NIBs).  Their similarity to conventional lithium-ion technol. is obvious; however, the cell chem. often significantly deviates.  Graphite, although being the std. neg. electrode in Li-ion batteries, is largely inactive for Na-ion storage in conventional non-aq. carbonate-based electrolytes, for example.  Very recently, it has been demonstrated that graphite can be activated for Na-ion storage in cells with ether-based electrolytes.  The storage mechanism is based on co-intercalation of solvent mols. along with the Na-ions, forming ternary graphite intercalation compds. (t-GICs).  This process is highly reversible but yet poorly understood.  Here, a comprehensive study is provided on the formation and the stability of t-GICs.  A series of ether solvents are being discussed: linear glymes with different chain lengths (mono-, di-, tri-, and tetraglyme), several derivs. with side groups as well as THF as a cyclic ether and one crown ether.  It is shown that the redox potentials shift depending on the ether chain length and mixing of ethers might enable tailoring of the redox behavior.  The inferior behavior of triglyme is likely due to the less ideal ion coordination.  Complementary expts. with lithium are made and demonstrate the superior behavior of sodium.  It was found that the increase in graphene layer spacing during intercalation only slightly depends on the chain length and is in the range of 250%, and still mech. stability is preserved.  It is further shown that the t-GICs possess chem. stability and demonstrated that the kinetically favored charge transfer is probably due to the absence of a solid electrolyte interphase.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGroQkB8YjSNVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTVlxWaAmUIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xlt1Oqsr0%253D&amp;md5=5d74083ea3e2c5f3295d3c0a5b355b85</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">534-541</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTVlxWaAmUIA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201405370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wickramaratne, N.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CuO Quantum Dots Embedded in Carbon Nanofibers as Binder-Free Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries with Enhanced Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiaojun; Liu, Yongchang; Wang, Yijing; Jiao, Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4865-4872</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The design of sodium ion batteries is proposed based on the use of flexible membrane composed of ultrasmall transition metal oxides.  In this paper, the prepn. of CuO quantum dots (≈2 nm) delicately embedded in carbon nanofibers (denoted as 2-CuO@C) with a thin film via a feasible electrospinning method is reported.  The CuO content can be controlled by altering the synthetic conditions and is optimized to 54 wt%.  As binder-free anode for sodium ion batteries, 2-CuO@C delivers an initial reversible capacity of 528 mA h/g at the c.d. of 100 mA/g, an exceptional rate capability of 250 mA h/g at 5000 mA/g, and an ultra-stable capacity of 401 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 500 mA/g.  The enhancement of electrochem. performance is attributed to the unique structure of 2-CuO@C, which offers a variety of advantages: highly conductive carbon matrix suppressing agglomeration of CuO grains, interconnected nanofibers ensuring short transport length for electrons, well-dispersed CuO quantum dots leading to highly utilization rate, and good mech. properties resulting in strong electrode integrity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoogoQcQ6j0ZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liQJHeePq2Ktw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVKgu7vP&amp;md5=bc4abeee5df0a98f8d12865d883b654b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Makaryan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Van Aken, K.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Disodium terephthalate (Na2C8H4O4) as high performance anode material for low-cost room-temperature sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Liang; Zhao, Junmei; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Zhou, Zhibin; Armand, Michel; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The carboxylate-based org. material, disodium terephthalate (Na2C8H4O4) is firstly introduced as a novel anode material for low-cost rechargeable room-temp. Na-ion batteries.  The material exhibits low Na insertion voltage at 0.29 V.  The Na2C8H4O4/KB composite electrode shows a reversible capacity of 250 mAh/g, corresponding to a two-electron transfer, with excellent cycling performance.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Terephthalate as an Organic Anode Material for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Yuwon; Shin, Dong-Seon; Woo, Seung Hee; Choi, Nam Soon; Shin, Kyung Hee; Oh, Seung M.; Lee, Kyu Tae; Hong, Sung You</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The org. electrode material, disodium terephthalate, was obtained using simple wet chem. - it showed excellent electrochem. performance, thus making it a promising candidate for Na ion batteries.  Capacity fading was negligible over many cycles and the rate performance was as good as commercialized electrode materials of lithium ion batteries, although the Na cation is 1.3 times larger than Li cation.  The redox potential was 0.4 V vs. Na/Na+, which is ideal for anode application with respect to safety and energy d.  Various derivs. of disodium terephthalate were easily synthesized and exhibited different electrochem. properties compared to disodium terephthalate.  These findings imply that the thermodn. and kinetic properties of org. electrodes can be controlled by the chem. modification of benzene-carboxylate scaffolding through the addn. of functional groups.  Because of the structural richness of the org. architecture, org. electrode materials may be utilized for next generation rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrQ4Z4S4AVgzLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liQJHeePq2Ktw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XotFynsrg%253D&amp;md5=37df019ccbeb888e0112ee2d0c4cecd4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201510978"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosted Charge Transfer in SnS/SnO<sub>2</sub> Heterostructures: Toward High Rate Capability for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing heterostructures can endow materials with fascinating performance in high-speed electronics, optoelectronics, and other applications owing to the built-in charge-transfer driving force, which is of benefit to the specific charge-transfer kinetics.  Rational design and controllable synthesis of nano-heterostructure anode materials with high-rate performance, however, still remains a great challenge.  Herein, ultrafine SnS/SnO2 heterostructures were successfully fabricated and showed enhanced charge-transfer capability.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb@C coaxial nanotubes as a superior long-life and high-rate anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhiming; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen; Paik, Ungyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2314-2318</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading which is largely due to the large vol. expansion during sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.  With different annealing time, the hollow space and the amt. of Sb inside the tube can be easily tuned by the partial evapn. of Sb.  The as-obtained Sb@C nanotubes exhibit excellent sodium storage properties.  The remarkable electrochem. performance results from the unique coaxial nanoarchitecture.  Specifically, it delivers a high specific capacity of 407 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 240 cycles.  Furthermore, a stable capacity of 240 mAh g-1 can be retained at 1.0 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles.  Most importantly, high capacities of 350 mAh g-1 and 310 mAh g-1 can be achieved at large current densities of 10 and 20 A g-1, resp., which represents the best rate performance among the reported Sb-based anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmon6HTiU9LrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lihWhIjbcR8ew"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus Nanodots on Reduced Graphene Oxide as a Flexible and Ultra-Fast Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Zhang, Anyi; Shen, Chenfei; Liu, Qingzhou; Cao, Xuan; Ma, Yuqiang; Chen, Liang; Lau, Christian; Chen, Tian-Chi; Wei, Fei; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5530-5537</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for potential low cost and large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na.  Red P is considered as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 2596 mA-h/g.  However, similar to Si in Li-ion batteries, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion upon sodiation/desodiation and low electronic conductance, have limited the performance of red P anodes.  To address the above challenges, the authors have developed a method to deposit red P nanodots densely and uniformly onto reduced graphene oxide sheets (P@RGO) to minimize the Na ion diffusion length and the sodiation/desodiation stresses, and the RGO network also serves as electron pathway and creates free space to accommodate the vol. variation of P particles.  The resulted P@RGO flexible anode achieved 1165.4, 510.6, and 135.3 mA-h/g specific charge capacity at 159.4, 31878.9, and 47818.3 mA/g charge/discharge c.d. in rate capability test, and a 914 mA-h/g capacity after 300 deep cycles in cycling stability test at 1593.9 mA/g c.d., which marks a significant performance improvement for red P anodes for Na-ion chem. and flexible power sources for wearable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9mlp0D8us-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lihWhIjbcR8ew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXot1ygtr8%253D&amp;md5=33417000c419534df3b536cd70b89933</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2014.35"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, G.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Black phosphorus field-effect transistors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Likai; Yu, Yijun; Ye, Guo Jun; Ge, Qingqin; Ou, Xuedong; Wu, Hua; Feng, Donglai; Chen, Xian Hui; Zhang, Yuanbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional crystals have emerged as a class of materials that may impact future electronic technologies.  Exptl. identifying and characterizing new functional two-dimensional materials is challenging, but also potentially rewarding.  Here, the authors fabricate field-effect transistors based on few-layer black phosphorus crystals with thickness down to a few nanometers.  Reliable transistor performance is achieved at room temp. in samples thinner than 7.5 nm, with drain current modulation ∼105 and well-developed current satn. in the I-V characteristics.  The charge-carrier mobility is thickness-dependent, with the highest values up to ∼1,000 cm2 V-1 s-1 obtained for a thickness of ∼10 nm.  The authors' results demonstrate the potential of black phosphorus thin crystals as a new two-dimensional material for applications in nanoelectronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqi8Ksk8pHsYbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lihWhIjbcR8ew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXjtlyht7c%253D&amp;md5=ade1fb1e245718cc47c0ca759b729e78</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C5CP01502B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kulish, V.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorene as an anode material for Na-ion batteries: a first-principles study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kulish, Vadym V.; Malyi, Oleksandr I.; Persson, Clas; Wu, Ping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We systematically investigate a novel two-dimensional nanomaterial, phosphorene, as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  Using first-principles calcns., we det. the Na adsorption energy, specific capacity and Na diffusion barriers on monolayer phosphorene.  We examine the main trends in the electronic structure and mech. properties as a function of Na concn.  We find a favorable Na-phosphorene interaction with a high theor. Na storage capacity.  We find that Na-phosphorene undergoes semiconductor-metal transition at high Na concn.  Our results show that Na diffusion on phosphorene is fast and anisotropic with an energy barrier of only 0.04 eV.  Owing to its high capacity, good stability, excellent elec. cond. and high Na mobility, monolayer phosphorene is a very promising anode material for Na-ion batteries.  The calcd. performance in terms of specific capacity and diffusion barriers is compared to other layered 2D electrode materials, such as graphene, MoS2, and polysilane.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQoKOjpBcSRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lihWhIjbcR8ew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXntVCit74%253D&amp;md5=14e2b43f2ed1622763e8ee63d0da4887</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1038/nnano.2015.194"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Phosphorene-Graphene Hybrid Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liz6jwd5tAdJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.6b01777"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured Black Phosphorus/Ketjenblack-Multiwalled Carbon Nanotubes Composite as High Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Gui-Liang; Chen, Zonghai; Zhong, Gui-Ming; Liu, Yuzi; Yang, Yong; Ma, Tianyuan; Ren, Yang; Zuo, Xiaobing; Wu, Xue-Hang; Zhang, Xiaoyi; Amine, Khalil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, the low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes for sodium-ion batteries are bottlenecks for future developments.  Here, we report a high performance nanostructured anode material for sodium-ion batteries that is fabricated by high energy ball milling to form black phosphorus/Ketjenblack-multiwalled carbon nanotubes (BPC) composite.  With this strategy, the BPC composite with a high phosphorus content (70 wt %) could deliver a very high initial Coulombic efficiency (&gt;90%) and high specific capacity with excellent cyclability at high rate of charge/discharge (∼1700 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 1.3 A g-1 based on the mass of P).                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Functionalized few-layer black phosphorus with super-wettability towards enhanced reaction kinetics for rechargeable batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yu; Sun, Wenping; Luo, Zhong-Zhen; Zheng, Yun; Yu, Zhenwei; Zhang, Dan; Yang, Jun; Tan, Hui Teng; Zhu, Jixin; Wang, Xiaolin; Yan, Qingyu; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Few-layer black phosphorus (BP) is a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity and favorable layered structure.  However, practical implementation is hindered by sluggish reaction kinetics and large vol. change during de/sodiation process.  Esp., combining BP with large portion of low-capacity carbonaceous materials is a common strategy to improve the Na storage properties, but leading to reduced specific capacity based on the overall mass of the whole electrode.  To address these challenges, nanoscale surface engineering of few-layer BP is herein performed by homogeneously depositing horizontally aligned Poly(3, 4-ethylenedioxythiophene) (PEDOT) nanofibers on specially surface-modified BP nanosheets.  Such material design could achieve simultaneously: (1) enhanced charge transfer kinetics and (2) super surface wettability with electrolyte.  Benefiting from the unique functionalization, the reaction kinetics are greatly enhanced accordingly for both sodium and lithium storage.  Our strategy sheds light on designing advanced electrodes for high-performance rechargeable batteries and other energy storage/conversion devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpnKZCaEeJs37Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liz6jwd5tAdJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVOjtrfF&amp;md5=bca1b8b8f7f077a69db69bfa693f7dc2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1021/cm021287x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baibarac, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Baltog, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lefrant, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mevellec, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chauvet, O.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyaniline and Carbon Nanotubes Based Composites Containing Whole Units and Fragments of Nanotubes</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Using surface-enhanced Raman scattering (SERS) and Fourier transform IR (FTIR) spectroscopy, we show that composites based on polyaniline (PANI) and single-walled carbon nanotubes (SWNTs) are different when they are prepd. by two different methods: (1) by adding dispersed SWNTs to the polymer solns. and (2) by chem. polymn. of aniline in the presence of SWNTs.  The difference originates from the irreversible chem. transformation of SWNTs in the polymn. medium.  The synthesis medium used for the prepn. of PANI transforms SWNTs into fragments of shorter length like closed-shell fullerenes.  This explains the similarity of SERS and FTIR spectra of the composites PANI/SWNTs and PANI/C60 chem. prepd.  All compds. exhibit an absorption band at 1144 cm-1 in their FTIR spectra, increasing with the carbon nanoparticles content, as a signature of a charge transfer between the constituents. Besides, the FTIR spectrum of the compds. obtained by adding SWNTs to the polymer soln. display an intense absorption band with two components at 773 and 755 cm-1, which are assocd. with the vibration of deformation of the benzene and the quinoid ring, resp.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic distribution in red and black phosphorus and the crystal structure of black phosphorus</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hultgren, Ralph; Gingrich, N. S.; Warren, B. E.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1935</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">No satisfactory crystal-structure detn. has been reported for any form of P.  Five samples of black P gave identical powder patterns different from those reported by Linck and Jung (C. A. 19, 3393), whose rhombohedral structure gives improbable interat. distances and co.ovrddot.ordination.  A sample prepd. at room temp. and 35,000 atm. gave the diffuse rings of an "amorphous" x-ray pattern.  Another sample, prepd. at 300° and 8000 atm., is a new form of P, with the same d. as black P.  At. distribution curves of cryst. and "amorphous" black and red P were obtained by Fourier analysis.  All 4 gave practically the same curve, showing 3 neighbors at 2.28 A. and about 12 at 3.6 A.  Black P consists of double layers; the cell is side-centered orthorhombic with a = 3.31 A., b = 4.38 A. and c = 10.50 A.  There are 8 atoms in the cell, giving a calcd. d. of 2.69 (observed d. 2.70).  The space group is Vh18-Bmab.  The black-P structure allows a closer packing than the As structure, where the at. environment is similar, and so is favored by the high pressure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqemH-aEKKRXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liz6jwd5tAdJQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaA2MXjvVGgsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=74dbe7a3f25ecd8cc24c2ed838204659</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/smll.200500513"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ducati, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Koziol, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Friedrichs, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yates, T.                 10.1021/jacs.8b02156</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D140%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D7561-7567%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DT.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BWan%26author%3DH.%2BXie%26author%3DY.%2BMu%26author%3DP.%2BDu%26author%3DD.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26author%3DH.%2BJi%26author%3DL.%2BWan%26title%3DDegradation%2BChemistry%2Band%2BStabilization%2Bof%2BExfoliated%2BFew-layer%2BBlack%2BPhosphorus%2Bin%2BWater%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjacs.8b02156&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b04088&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjacs.8b02156&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Degradation Chemistry and Stabilization of Exfoliated Few-Layer Black Phosphorus in Water</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Taiming; Wan, Yangyang; Xie, Huanyu; Mu, Yang; Du, Pingwu; Wang, Dong; Wu, Xiaojun; Ji, Hengxing; Wan, Lijun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">140</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7561-7567</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exfoliated black phosphorus (BP), as a monolayer or few-layer material, has attracted tremendous attention owing to its unique phys. properties for applications ranging from optoelectronics to photocatalytic hydrogen prodn.  Approaching intrinsic properties has been, however, challenged by chem. reactions and structure degrdn. of BP under ambient conditions.  Surface passivation by capping agents has been proposed to extend the processing time window, yet contamination or structure damage rise challenges for BP applications.  Here, we report expts. combined with first-principle calcns. that address the degrdn. chem. of BP.  Our results show that BP reacts with oxygen in water even without light illumination.  The reaction follows a pseudo-first-order parallel reaction kinetics, produces PO23-, PO33-, and PO43- with reaction rate consts. of 0.019, 0.034, and 0.023 per day, resp., and occurs preferentially from the P atoms locating at BP edges, which yields structural decay from the nanoflake edges in water.  In addn., a negligible decay ratio (0.9 ± 0.3 mol %) and preserved photocatalytic activity of BP are obsd. after storage in deoxygenated water for 15 days without surface passivation under ambient light.  Our results reveal the chem. of BP degrdn. and provide a practical approach for exfoliation, delivery, and application of BP.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowRb6CMoWLC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg6FMNPn10vQg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXlvVKnsbc%253D&amp;md5=9af29f8740aee5a3b9c8d450588501df</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da90f79dcdb325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A rather general strategy to prep. self-supported interpenetrating 3D tricontinuous cathodes that is based on the facile electrostatic spray deposition (ESD) technique is proposed.  Taking Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) as a model system, interconnected 3D tricontinuous NVP:rGO-CNT (reduced graphene oxide-carbon nanotube) is directly deposited on the current collector without any conductive additives or binders usually needed for battery assembling.  A full sodium battery using such interpenetrating 3D tricontinuous NVP:rGO-CNT as both cathode and anode has been successfully constructed, demonstrating a reversible capacity of ~90 mAh g-1 at 10 C with an output voltage plateau of ~1.7 V and connected with energy d. of ~150 Wh kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpdNVL3mynqA7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPvomDERMORA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhtl2nu7w%253D&amp;md5=730ba202c36166725f79c8d03e86ad34</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5358"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barpanda, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oyama, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishimura, S.-i.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, S.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A 3.8-V Earth-Abundant Sodium Battery Electrode</span>. <i>Nat.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable lithium batteries have ushered the wireless revolution over last two decades and are now matured to enable green automobiles.  However, the growing concern on scarcity and large-scale applications of lithium resources have steered effort to realize sustainable sodium-ion batteries, Na and Fe being abundant and low-cost charge carrier and redox center, resp.  However, their performance is limited owing to low operating voltage and sluggish kinetics.  Here we report a hitherto-unknown material with entirely new compn. and structure with the first alluaudite-type sulfate framework, Na2Fe2(SO4)3, registering the highest-ever Fe3+/Fe2+ redox potential at 3.8 V (vs. Na, and hence 4.1 V vs. Li) along with fast rate kinetics.  Rare-metal-free Na-ion rechargeable battery system compatible with the present Li-ion battery is now in realistic scope without sacrificing high energy d. and high power, and paves way for discovery of new earth-abundant sustainable cathodes for large-scale batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_sUr2Jpgw1LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgPvomDERMORA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVShs77L&amp;md5=20951f27b1483820983947a5d84d607f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms6280"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Manganese hexacyanomanganate open framework as a high-capacity positive electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Hyun-Wook; Wang, Richard Y.; Pasta, Mauro; Lee, Seok Woo; Liu, Nian; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potential applications of sodium-ion batteries in grid-scale energy storage, portable electronics and elec. vehicles have revitalized research interest in these batteries.  However, the performance of sodium-ion electrode materials has not been competitive with that of lithium-ion electrode materials.  Here we present sodium manganese hexacyanomanganate (Na2MnII[MnII(CN)6]), an open-framework crystal structure material, as a viable pos. electrode for sodium-ion batteries.  We demonstrate a high discharge capacity of 209 mAh g-1 at C/5 (40 mA g-1) and excellent capacity retention at high rates in a propylene carbonate electrolyte.  We provide chem. and structural evidence for the unprecedented storage of 50% more sodium cations than previously thought possible during electrochem. cycling.  These results represent a step forward in the development of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodYRgprGozjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGtIxFNXjTOg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVemsrg%253D&amp;md5=24c6dc57b45017370f872c3c6723f4c4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/C6CP00651E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jache, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Binder, J. O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abe, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adelhelm, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Comparative Study on the Impact of Different Glymes and Their Derivatives as Electrolyte Solvents for Graphite Co-intercalation Electrodes in Lithium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Phys. Chem. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14299</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14316</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6CP00651E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comparative study on the impact of different glymes and their derivatives as electrolyte solvents for graphite co-intercalation electrodes in lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jache, Birte; Binder, Jan Oliver; Abe, Takeshi; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14299-14316</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundance of sodium has recently sparked considerable interest in sodium-ion batteries (NIBs).  Their similarity to conventional lithium-ion technol. is obvious; however, the cell chem. often significantly deviates.  Graphite, although being the std. neg. electrode in Li-ion batteries, is largely inactive for Na-ion storage in conventional non-aq. carbonate-based electrolytes, for example.  Very recently, it has been demonstrated that graphite can be activated for Na-ion storage in cells with ether-based electrolytes.  The storage mechanism is based on co-intercalation of solvent mols. along with the Na-ions, forming ternary graphite intercalation compds. (t-GICs).  This process is highly reversible but yet poorly understood.  Here, a comprehensive study is provided on the formation and the stability of t-GICs.  A series of ether solvents are being discussed: linear glymes with different chain lengths (mono-, di-, tri-, and tetraglyme), several derivs. with side groups as well as THF as a cyclic ether and one crown ether.  It is shown that the redox potentials shift depending on the ether chain length and mixing of ethers might enable tailoring of the redox behavior.  The inferior behavior of triglyme is likely due to the less ideal ion coordination.  Complementary expts. with lithium are made and demonstrate the superior behavior of sodium.  It was found that the increase in graphene layer spacing during intercalation only slightly depends on the chain length and is in the range of 250%, and still mech. stability is preserved.  It is further shown that the t-GICs possess chem. stability and demonstrated that the kinetically favored charge transfer is probably due to the absence of a solid electrolyte interphase.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGroQkB8YjSNVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGtIxFNXjTOg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xlt1Oqsr0%253D&amp;md5=5d74083ea3e2c5f3295d3c0a5b355b85</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.                         rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage Behavior in Natural Graphite using Ether-based Electrolyte Systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Hong, Jihyun; Park, Young-Uk; Kim, Jinsoo; Hwang, Insang; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports that natural graphite is capable of Na insertion and extn. with a remarkable reversibility using ether-based electrolytes.  Natural graphite (the most well-known anode material for Li-ion batteries) has been barely studied as a suitable anode for Na rechargeable batteries due to the lack of Na intercalation capability.  Herein, graphite is not only capable of Na intercalation but also exhibits outstanding performance as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  The graphite anode delivers a reversible capacity of ≈150 mA-h/g with a cycle stability for 2500 cycles, and more than 75 mA-h/g at 10 A/g despite its micrometer-size (≈100 μm).  An Na storage mechanism in graphite, where Na+-solvent co-intercalation occurs combined with partial pseudocapacitive behaviors, is shown.  It is demonstrated that the electrolyte solvent species significantly affect the electrochem. properties, not only rate capability but also redox potential.  The feasibility of graphite in a Na full cell is also confirmed in conjunction with the Na1.5VPO4.8F0.7 cathode, delivering an energy of ≈120 W-h/kg while maintaining ≈70% of the initial capacity after 250 cycles.  This exceptional behavior of natural graphite promises new avenues for the development of cost-effective and reliable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpH2c5ZOoUcVbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGtIxFNXjTOg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGiurrN&amp;md5=0bb4c36145b59a3b9727155eca307655</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201405370"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wickramaratne, N.                         rightTab-cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">CuO Quantum Dots Embedded in Carbon Nanofibers as Binder-Free Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries with Enhanced Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiaojun; Liu, Yongchang; Wang, Yijing; Jiao, Lifang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The design of sodium ion batteries is proposed based on the use of flexible membrane composed of ultrasmall transition metal oxides.  In this paper, the prepn. of CuO quantum dots (≈2 nm) delicately embedded in carbon nanofibers (denoted as 2-CuO@C) with a thin film via a feasible electrospinning method is reported.  The CuO content can be controlled by altering the synthetic conditions and is optimized to 54 wt%.  As binder-free anode for sodium ion batteries, 2-CuO@C delivers an initial reversible capacity of 528 mA h/g at the c.d. of 100 mA/g, an exceptional rate capability of 250 mA h/g at 5000 mA/g, and an ultra-stable capacity of 401 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 500 mA/g.  The enhancement of electrochem. performance is attributed to the unique structure of 2-CuO@C, which offers a variety of advantages: highly conductive carbon matrix suppressing agglomeration of CuO grains, interconnected nanofibers ensuring short transport length for electrons, well-dispersed CuO quantum dots leading to highly utilization rate, and good mech. properties resulting in strong electrode integrity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoogoQcQ6j0ZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5W3hkHlO7-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVKgu7vP&amp;md5=bc4abeee5df0a98f8d12865d883b654b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Makaryan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Van Aken, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing heterostructures can endow materials with fascinating performance in high-speed electronics, optoelectronics, and other applications owing to the built-in charge-transfer driving force, which is of benefit to the specific charge-transfer kinetics.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony (Sb) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 660 mAh g-1. Tuning the morphol. and structure at the nanoscale or using carbonaceous materials as the buffer layer is essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile carbon-coating coupled with a thermal-redn. strategy has been developed to synthesize unique Sb@C coaxial nanotubes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for potential low cost and large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na. However, similar to Si in Li-ion batteries, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion upon sodiation/desodiation and low electronic conductance, have limited the performance of red P anodes.  To address the above challenges, the authors have developed a method to deposit red P nanodots densely and uniformly onto reduced graphene oxide sheets (P@RGO) to minimize the Na ion diffusion length and the sodiation/desodiation stresses, and the RGO network also serves as electron pathway and creates free space to accommodate the vol. variation of P particles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional crystals have emerged as a class of materials that may impact future electronic technologies.  Exptl. identifying and characterizing new functional two-dimensional materials is challenging, but also potentially rewarding.  Here, the authors fabricate field-effect transistors based on few-layer black phosphorus crystals with thickness down to a few nanometers.  Reliable transistor performance is achieved at room temp. in samples thinner than 7.5 nm, with drain current modulation ∼105 and well-developed current satn. in the I-V characteristics.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We systematically investigate a novel two-dimensional nanomaterial, phosphorene, as an anode for Na-ion batteries.  Using first-principles calcns., we det. the Na adsorption energy, specific capacity and Na diffusion barriers on monolayer phosphorene.  We examine the main trends in the electronic structure and mech. properties as a function of Na concn.  We find a favorable Na-phosphorene interaction with a high theor. Na storage capacity.  We find that Na-phosphorene undergoes semiconductor-metal transition at high Na concn.  Our results show that Na diffusion on phosphorene is fast and anisotropic with an energy barrier of only 0.04 eV.  Owing to its high capacity, good stability, excellent elec. cond. and high Na mobility, monolayer phosphorene is a very promising anode material for Na-ion batteries. Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Few-layer black phosphorus (BP) is a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity and favorable layered structure.  However, practical implementation is hindered by sluggish reaction kinetics and large vol. change during de/sodiation process.  Esp., combining BP with large portion of low-capacity carbonaceous materials is a common strategy to improve the Na storage properties, but leading to reduced specific capacity based on the overall mass of the whole electrode.  To address these challenges, nanoscale surface engineering of few-layer BP is herein performed by homogeneously depositing horizontally aligned Poly(3, 4-ethylenedioxythiophene) (PEDOT) nanofibers on specially surface-modified BP nanosheets.  Such material design could achieve simultaneously: (1) enhanced charge transfer kinetics and (2) super surface wettability with electrolyte. A. 19, 3393), whose rhombohedral structure gives improbable interat. distances and co.ovrddot.ordination.  A sample prepd. at room temp. and 35,000 atm. gave the diffuse rings of an "amorphous" x-ray pattern.  Another sample, prepd. at 300° and 8000 atm., is a new form of P, with the same d. as black P.  At. distribution curves of cryst. and "amorphous" black and red P were obtained by Fourier analysis.  All 4 gave practically the same curve, showing 3 neighbors at 2.28 A. and about 12 at 3.6 A.  Black P consists of double layers; the cell is side-centered orthorhombic with a = 3.31 A., b = 4.38 A. and c = 10.50 A.  There are 8 atoms in the cell, giving a calcd. d. of 2.69 (observed d. 2.70).  The space group is Vh18-Bmab.  The black-P structure allows a closer packing than the As structure, where the at. environment is similar, and so is favored by the high pressure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqemH-aEKKRXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgtJeiG5tP-eA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaA2MXjvVGgsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=74dbe7a3f25ecd8cc24c2ed838204659</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/smll.200500513"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ducati, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Koziol, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Friedrichs, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yates, T.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Multi-walled C nanotubes were synthesized by CVD from pure toluene and toluene/diazine mixts. using ferrocene as a catalyst precursor at 760°.  As recently announced, characterization of the resulting nanotube films showed that, unlike pure C nanotubes, those grown in the presence of N2 have an extremely high degree of internal order, both in terms of the uniform chirality in the nanotube walls and of the crystallog. register between them.  Here, the structure, defects, and morphol. of the nanotubes were analyzed in depth using advanced electron microscopy techniques, and compared with existing models and observations.  N, which seems to be responsible for the dramatic structural order, was found to segregate preferentially within the core of the nanotubes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpGIAy1rSsNBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMNdo6k6p86Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XkslOmsbk%253D&amp;md5=850359468f1d1ce5b354404a33be82a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1016/S0368-2048(98)00423-X"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cavell, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">P 1s photoabsorption spectra of gaseous trivalent and pentavalent P compds. scanning coordination nos. 3, 4 and 5 were measured using synchrotron radiation. The main pre-edge peak shifts with chem. substitution and edge differences (relative to PH3) were analyzed in terms of simple potential and charge models.  Comparing these shifts with those of corresponding photoelectron and Auger shifts indicates that similar structural and electronic effects operate.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq5bsbBcbNUzrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMNdo6k6p86Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK1MXjvFWgu7c%253D&amp;md5=53babb04b0870570699c1f3ac6cb954f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700431"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges and Perspectives for NASICON-Type Electrode Materials for Advanced Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H. J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>/Conductive-Polymer Core/Shell Nanobelt Array on Three-Dimensional Graphite Foam: A High-Rate, Ultrastable, and Freestanding Cathode for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have designed and successfully fabricated a V205/PEDOT core/shell nanobelt array (NBA) on ultra thin graphite foam (UFG) as self-supported,binder-free pos. electrodes.  This is the first time that direct growth of V2O5 nanoarrays on current collectors has been realized.  Such integrated electrodes exhibit ultrafast and stable Li ion storage performance, with higher capacities and improved rate and cycling capabilities than the bare V2O5 NBA on UFG.  High specific capacities of 265 mA h g-1 at 5 C and 168 mA hĝ 1 at 60 C are achieved, which can maintain 98 % of their values up to 1000 cycles.  The key role of the PEDOT shell is explained as facilitating the charge transfer and hence the reaction kinetics, and also preserving the NBA structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqptiuCrkG9brVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMNdo6k6p86Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXovFKltbg%253D&amp;md5=7fe34806725ec8135be14d3e6b442ad2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/jacs.8b02156"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wan, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Degradation Chemistry and Stabilization of Exfoliated Few-layer Black Phosphorus in Water</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>140</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">7561</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7567</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.8b02156</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Degradation Chemistry and Stabilization of Exfoliated Few-Layer Black Phosphorus in Water</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Taiming; Wan, Yangyang; Xie, Huanyu; Mu, Yang; Du, Pingwu; Wang, Dong; Wu, Xiaojun; Ji, Hengxing; Wan, Lijun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">140</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7561-7567</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exfoliated black phosphorus (BP), as a monolayer or few-layer material, has attracted tremendous attention owing to its unique phys. properties for applications ranging from optoelectronics to photocatalytic hydrogen prodn.  Approaching intrinsic properties has been, however, challenged by chem. reactions and structure degrdn. of BP under ambient conditions.  Surface passivation by capping agents has been proposed to extend the processing time window, yet contamination or structure damage rise challenges for BP applications.  Here, we report expts. combined with first-principle calcns. that address the degrdn. chem. of BP.  Our results show that BP reacts with oxygen in water even without light illumination.  The reaction follows a pseudo-first-order parallel reaction kinetics, produces PO23-, PO33-, and PO43- with reaction rate consts. of 0.019, 0.034, and 0.023 per day, resp., and occurs preferentially from the P atoms locating at BP edges, which yields structural decay from the nanoflake edges in water.  In addn., a negligible decay ratio (0.9 ± 0.3 mol %) and preserved photocatalytic activity of BP are obsd. after storage in deoxygenated water for 15 days without surface passivation under ambient light.  Our results reveal the chem. of BP degrdn. and provide a practical approach for exfoliation, delivery, and application of BP.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowRb6CMoWLC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMNdo6k6p86Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXlvVKnsbc%253D&amp;md5=9af29f8740aee5a3b9c8d450588501df</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i11">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.9b04088" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.9b04088</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">SEM and TEM images of BP, BP-G, and BP-/PANI; (function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

<script nonce="90da90f79dcdb325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
